033-149. Program-written effect `desired:` cells default to `cross_thread_snapshot`. (§15.4.1.4)
033-150. Stdlib single-cell types per §13.12.4 default to `cross_thread_atomic`. (§15.4.1.4)
033-151. Local `let`/`mut` bindings inside function bodies are non-reactive and do not appear in the graph specification. (§15.4.1.4)
033-152. Closure captures and function parameters do not appear in the graph specification. (§15.4.1.4)
033-153. The compiler may downgrade `cross_thread_snapshot` to `confined` for cells provably accessed from only one thread; this optimization is implementation-defined. (§15.4.1.4)
033-154. The compiler may never upgrade a cell's observability class (e.g., `confined` to `cross_thread_snapshot`). (§15.4.1.4)
033-155. Cells declared inside placements that participate in the runtime's evaluation cycle default to `cadence_hint` `realtime`. (§15.4.1.4)
033-156. Cells on non-realtime paths default to `cadence_hint` `bounded`. (§15.4.1.4)
033-157. A conformant runtime accepts any specification whose format version it understands. (§15.4.2)
033-158. Format-version mismatches are diagnosed at load time per §14.9. (§15.4.2)
033-159. The specification is type-erased at the runtime boundary: it carries primitive type tags and cell layouts but no record definitions, trait conformances, or generic parameters. (§15.4.3)
033-160. Record definitions, trait conformances, and generic parameters are compile-time artifacts of the frontend, fully resolved before the specification is emitted. (§15.4.3)
033-161. The runtime's view of the program is a graph of cells with primitive types, dependency edges, behavior references, and gate predicates. (§15.4.3)
033-162. The runtime manages bits in cells and invokes functions by ID; it never needs to understand records as records or traits as traits. (§15.4.3)
033-163. A behavior is a pure function the runtime invokes to compute a derived value, a gate predicate, or an effect's desired state. (§15.4.4)
033-164. The behavior IR is typed: every value has a concrete type from the §15.4 vocabulary. (§15.4.4)
033-165. The behavior IR is SSA: each value is assigned once and control flow is basic blocks. (§15.4.4)
033-166. There are no phi nodes; a block needing a merged value declares it as a block parameter: `bb1(%k: i32):`. (§15.4.4)
033-167. The behavior IR is monomorphic; generics are already specialized: `push$Vec_i32`. (§15.4.4)
033-168. The behavior IR is ownership-explicit: `move`, `clone`, and `drop` are written out, never inferred. (§15.4.4)
033-169. A behavior is pure: a function of its declared inputs only, with no ambient state and no I/O. (§15.4.4)
033-170. I/O is the domain of effects, which are graph-level, never of behaviors. (§15.4.4)
033-171. A behavior may compute, allocate, call other behaviors, and `trap`. (§15.4.4)
033-172. Behaviors are total except `trap`: the only non-`ret` exit is `trap`. (§15.4.4)
033-173. A behavior's signature is `behavior <id> (params) -> <type> { block+ }`. (§15.4.4)
033-174. A behavior parameter `p: T` is borrow-default: read, not consumed. (§15.4.4)
033-175. A behavior parameter `own p: T` is consumed. (§15.4.4)
033-176. The entry block's parameters are the behavior's parameters. (§15.4.4)
033-177. A branch supplies its successor block's arguments, replacing phi: `cond_br flag, bb1(%0), bb2`. (§15.4.4)
033-178. Constant instructions are typed: `const.i32 5`, `const.f64 3.14`, `const.bool true`, `const.str "…"`. (§15.4.4)
033-179. The arithmetic/bitwise instructions are `add sub mul div rem neg and or xor shl shr not`, with typed variants implied by `.iN`/`.fN` suffixes. (§15.4.4)
033-180. Overflow in behavior-IR arithmetic follows the rules of §4. (§15.4.4)
033-181. The comparison instructions `eq ne lt le gt ge` produce `bool`. (§15.4.4)
033-182. Conversions are explicit per §7.5: `cast.<from>.<to> %x`. (§15.4.4)
033-183. The aggregate instructions are `tuple.make`/`tuple.get`, `record.make %T {…}`/`field.get`, `enum.make %T #V(p)`/`enum.tag`/`enum.payload`, and `array.make […]`. (§15.4.4)
033-184. Field/index assignment is a trait `call`, not an IR primitive, so in-place reuse follows the ordinary ownership rules. (§15.4.4)
033-185. Direct calls are statically resolved: `call f(move %a, %b)`. (§15.4.4)
033-186. `call.dyn %obj #m (…)` is the vtable call on a `dyn` trait object. (§15.4.4)
033-187. `call.closure %c (…)` invokes a closure. (§15.4.4)
033-188. `closure.make B@id captures {…}` constructs a closure. (§15.4.4)
033-189. `dyn` and closure calls are the only indirect call forms; the frontend resolves all other dispatch to direct calls. (§15.4.4)
033-190. `move` is an operand modifier at call arguments, stores, and returns. (§15.4.4)
033-191. `clone` duplicates a value: `%c = clone %x`. (§15.4.4)
033-192. `drop %x` marks explicit end-of-life. (§15.4.4)
033-193. The intrinsics are `raw_alloc<T>(%n)`, `raw_free(move %b)`, `raw_read<T>`, `raw_write<T>`, and `trap "msg"`. (§15.4.4)
033-194. The intrinsics are the fixed primitive floor: the only operations not expressible in Ductus, available to every program equally. (§15.4.4)
033-195. Stdlib collections are ordinary behaviors built on the intrinsics; no privileged operations exist. (§15.4.4)
033-196. Every behavior block ends in exactly one terminator. (§15.4.4)
033-197. `br bbN(args)` is the unconditional branch terminator. (§15.4.4)
033-198. `cond_br %c, bbT(args), bbF(args)` is the conditional branch terminator. (§15.4.4)
033-199. `switch %tag [0:bb0, 1:bb1, default:bbd]` is the multi-way terminator. (§15.4.4)
033-200. `match` lowers to `enum.tag` plus `switch`. (§15.4.4)
033-201. `ret %v` is the value-returning terminator. (§15.4.4)
033-202. `trap "msg"` is a terminator. (§15.4.4)
033-203. Recoverable failures (`Result`/`Option`, `?`) are ordinary values plus `switch`. (§15.4.4)
033-204. Unrecoverable failures — `panic`, overflow, failed index — are `trap`: process abort, not catchable. (§15.4.4)
033-205. Surface-construct lowerings introduce no new IR primitives. (§15.4.4)
033-206. A `for`/iterator loop lowers to a block calling `next` (tuple-return) plus a `switch` on the `Option`. (§15.4.4)
033-207. The linear-ownership in-place loop optimization is the dead-`move`-plus-rebind pattern (§11.11.2, §12.7.2). (§15.4.4)
033-208. `?` and string interpolation desugar to plain `switch`/`call` sequences. (§15.4.4)
033-209. An `observe` expression lowers to a derived read. (§15.4.4)
033-210. A closure's captured environment has a layout recorded as a `%TypeId` in the `types` table. (§15.4.4)
033-211. A newtype lowers to a `%TypeId` wrapper, or is transparent to its wrapped tag. (§15.4.4)
033-212. The runtime invokes a behavior by id with input values and receives outputs; it never reaches inside. (§15.4.4)
033-213. A derived behavior's inputs are its cell's input cells as current snapshot values; its output is the new value. (§15.4.4)
033-214. A recurrent behavior's inputs are its input cells, self-history slots (`name.past(k,d)` becomes a `pastK` param), and input-history slots (`input.past(k)` becomes an `<input>_pastK` param); its output is the new value. (§15.4.4)
033-215. A gate-predicate behavior's inputs are the gate's input cells; its output is `bool`, or a tag for a `given` selector. (§15.4.4)
033-216. An effect desired-builder behavior's inputs are the `desired:` block's input cells; its output is the desired record. (§15.4.4)
033-217. ABI inputs are passed per the signature's ownership modes (borrow vs `own`). (§15.4.4)
033-218. The ABI call is the entire graph-to-behavior coupling: behaviors hold no wiring, the graph holds no logic. (§15.4.4)
033-219. The text grammar's behavior production is: `behavior ::= 'behavior' BID '(' params ')' '->' type '{' block+ '}'`. (§15.4.4)
033-220. The text grammar's params production is: `params ::= (('own')? NAME ':' type) (',' …)*`. (§15.4.4)
033-221. The text grammar's block production is: `block ::= LABEL ('(' params ')')? ':' instr* terminator`. (§15.4.4)
033-222. The text grammar's instruction production is: `instr ::= '%'NAME '=' op operand* (':' type)? | op operand*`. (§15.4.4)
033-223. The text grammar's operand production is: `operand ::= '%'NAME | 'move' '%'NAME | literal`. (§15.4.4)
033-224. An effect's desired computation has no activation input anywhere; activation is expressed solely through the suspend/resume model (§13.19.12). (§15.4.5)
033-225. Interpreter and native modes share the entire frontend and differ only in the executable-code artifact. (§15.5)
033-226. The spec does not specify the interpreter bytecode format or the per-mode build pipeline. (§15.5)
033-227. Mode selection and toolchain integration are implementation concerns. (§15.5)
033-228. Hot reload diffs the graph specifications of two builds of the same program (`old_spec` vs `new_spec`); the diff computes the changes the runtime applies. (§15.6)
033-229. The diff classifies the overall change set per §13.15.4 into one of three categories: reload-safe, per-instance restart required, or full-runtime restart required. (§15.6.1)
033-230. Reload-safe changes are applied in place per §14.8. (§15.6.1)
033-231. Per-instance restart means operator-specific reinit per §13.17.10. (§15.6.1)
033-232. Full-runtime restart is required for buffer-layout relocation per §13.15.4. (§15.6.1)
033-233. Reload classification is computed from the diff alone; the runtime does not re-parse source. (§15.6.1)
033-234. The diff produces a reload plan: a sequenced list of cell add/remove/change, connection add/remove/change, and behavior add/remove operations the runtime applies in topological order. (§15.6.2)
033-235. The reload-plan format is implementation-defined. (§15.6.2)
033-236. A reload plan must preserve the ordering constraints of §14.7 (drop in reverse-declaration order; connections before endpoint instances) and §14.8. (§15.6.2)
033-237. An implementation comprises a compiler and a runtime operating on the same graph specification format; conformance requires both components to meet their criteria. (§15.7)
033-238. A conformant compiler accepts every program that §§1–13 define as well-formed. (§15.7.1)
033-239. A conformant compiler rejects every ill-formed program, with diagnostics whose format is implementation-defined. (§15.7.1)
033-240. A conformant compiler produces an IR conforming to the abstract data model of §15.4.1, with any serialization implementation-defined. (§15.7.1)
033-241. A conformant compiler's executable code, run against a conformant runtime with the produced graph specification, exhibits the observable behavior defined by §§1–13. (§15.7.1)
033-242. A conformant runtime accepts any IR conforming to the §15.4.1 abstract data model, in whatever serialization the implementations share. (§15.7.2)
033-243. A conformant runtime allocates cells per the observability and cadence contracts, using any mechanism that satisfies them. (§15.7.2)
033-244. A conformant runtime implements the runtime semantics of §13 and §14: cell evaluation order, drop semantics, hot reload, and thread orchestration. (§15.7.2)
033-245. Interoperability is defined against the IR's text form. (§15.7.3)
033-246. Two implementations exchanging a serialization must load it at the same format version. (§15.7.3)
033-247. Mixing a compiler from one implementation with a runtime from another is permitted at the same schema and format version. (§15.7.3)
033-248. The spec prescribes no reference test suite. (§15.7.4)
033-249. Implementations may publish conformance suites; passing such a suite is not a normative requirement. (§15.7.4)
